# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Prometheus TSDB Head Series Limit Exceeded

## Your Task

Prometheus crashes with 'out of bound samples' when cardinality is high. Find the Go source files in prometheus/prometheus that (1) enforce the head block series limit and (2) handle out-of-order or out-of-bound samples in the TSDB head.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json

  ],

    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've successfully completed the analysis and created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`. 

## Summary

I've identified the Go source files in the `prometheus/prometheus` repository that handle head block series limits and out-of-order/out-of-bounds sample validation:

### Key Files:
1. **`tsdb/head.go`** - Defines the Head block structure and enforces series creation limits through the `SeriesLifecycleCallback` interface
2. **`tsdb/head_append.go`** - Contains the core append logic with fast-path rejection and detailed per-series validation
3. **`tsdb/head_append_v2.go`** - Newer appender implementation with similar validation
4. **`tsdb/ooo_head.go`** - Handles out-of-order sample storage when OOO support is enabled
5. **`storage/interface.go`** - Defines error types for rejection conditions

### Key Mechanisms:
- **Series Limit Enforcement**: The `getOrCreateWithOptionalID()` function in head.go calls `SeriesLifecycleCallback.PreCreation()` to allow external callers to enforce cardinality limits
- **Out-of-Bounds Validation**: Samples with timestamps before `minValidTime` are rejected with `ErrOutOfBounds` when OOO support is disabled
- **Out-of-Order Handling**: The `appendable()` function determines if samples can go in in-order chunks, OOO chunks, or should be rejected based on timestamp and configuration
- **Histogram Support**: Separate validation functions handle histogram and float histogram samples with the same logic

The answer file includes detailed line numbers, function signatures, and a complete narrative explaining how the system prevents crashes from high cardinality by rejecting out-of-order and out-of-bounds samples.

\\n17: `HeadSeriesRef` is simply a 64bit counter that increments when a new series comes in.\\n18: Due to series churn, the set of actively used `HeadSeriesRef`s may be well above zero (e.g. 0-10M may not be used, and 10M-11M is active)\\n19: \\n20: \",\"endLine\":20,\"startLine\":14},{\"content\":\"25: Notes:\\n26: 1) M-mapped Head chunks, while they use `HeadSeriesRef`s, don't contain an index labels for those `HeadSeriesRef`s.             "content": "76: \n77: #### Why does `HeadChunkRef` contain a series reference and `BlockChunkRef` does not?\n78: \n79: ",

          {
            "content": "14: \n15: #### `HeadSeriesRef`\n16: \n17: `HeadSeriesRef` is simply a 64bit counter that increments when a new series comes in.\n18: Due to series churn, the set of actively used `HeadSeriesRef`s may be well above zero (e.g. 0-10M may not be used, and 10M-11M is active)\n19: \n20: ",
            "endLine": 20,
            "startLine": 14
          },
          {
            "content": "25: Notes:\n26: 1) M-mapped Head chunks, while they use `HeadSeriesRef`s, don't contain an index and depend on the series listing in memory.\n27: Once mmapped, chunks have `HeadSeriesRef`s inside them, allowing you to recreate the index from reading chunks\n28: (Along with WAL which has the labels for those `HeadSeriesRef`s. It also has all those samples, but by using m-mapped chunks we can save cpu/time and not replay all of WAL on startup)\n29: \n30: 2) During querying, `HeadSeriesRef` are limited to 2^40 (see `HeadChunkRef`)\n31: \n32: 3) The last `HeadSeriesRef` is always replayed from the WAL and is continued from there.\n33: \n34: #### `BlockSeriesRef`\n35: \n36: Persistent blocks are independent entities and the format/structure is completely different from head block.\n37: \n38: In blocks, series are lexicographically ordered by labels and the byte offset in the index file (divided by 16 because they're all aligned on 16 bytes) becomes the `BlockSeriesRef`.\n39: \n40: ",
            "endLine": 40,

          {
            "content": "238: data over a long range of times, it may be advantageous to use a larger value for\n239: the block duration to backfill faster and prevent additional compactions by TSDB later.\n240: \n241: The `--max-block-duration` flag allows the user to configure a maximum duration of blocks.\n242: The backfilling tool will pick a suitable block duration no larger than this.\n243: \n244: While larger blocks may improve the performance of backfilling large datasets,\n245: drawbacks exist as well. This structure maintains separate chunks for out-of-order samples that don't fit the normal in-order append pattern, allowing Prometheus to handle late-arriving samples from distributed systems.\\n\\nThe validation chain flows: Append() \u2192 getOrCreate() [series creation with PreCreation callback] \u2192 appendable() [sample timestamp validation] \u2192 storage in in-order or OOO chunks depending on timestamp and configuration.\"\n}\n",
